The study employs a stochastic model for gambi African trypanosomiasis (gH) in the Democratic Republic of Congo’s Mosango zone, using particle Markov chain Monte Carlo to fit six health areas. Deterministic models are faster but similar; stochastic better capture uncertainty. Kinamba, with third of cases, latest. Recommend deterministic for large-scale, stochastic for projections. First model fitted to data, enabling targeted interventions.
Researchers developed a method using spatial K functions and functional data analysis with random forests to predict cancer outcomes and identify key TME interactions in TNBC and lung, validated via simulations and MIB data, available in 'fycells R package.
The study investigates how neuronal dynamics, synaptic weights, and structural plasticity co-evolve during synchronization and desynchronization, using computational models of excitatory integrate-and-fire neurons with four plasticity regimes: STDP-only, homeostatic structural plasticity (hSP), STDP+hSP, and STDP+SP (including weight pruning). Structural reorganization, particularly weight-dependent pruning, enhances synchrony with sparser connections by strengthening high-to-low firing rate neuron links and removing weak synapses, creating degree correlations. STDP-only networks desynchronize with lower stimuli than ST+hSP/STDPSP models, which require higher intensity for long-term effects. Findings suggest structural plasticity impacts network resilience to external perturbations, informing non-invasive/invasive therapies for disorders like Parkinson’s. Stochastic SP model aligns with neurobiological methods but is computationally efficient.
Planarians regenerate neurons and glia from distinct progenitors, with Delta-2-expressing neurons instructing phagocytic progenitors (Notch1+) to differentiate into glia. Delta-2 inhibition reduces glia but not phagocytes; transplanted Delta-2 neurons induce ectopic glia. Model: Delta-Notch coordinates regen, enabling modular glial evolution. Notch in glial spec distinct from neuronal. Coordinated via neuron-phag signaling. (1030 words)
This study investigated gamma-delta (γδ) T cell responses before and during acute HIV infection (AHI) in individuals who later developed broadly neutralizing antibodies (bNAbs) versus those who did not. γδ T cell surface markers, particularly CD6 on Vδ1 T and CD5 on V2 T cells, were higher in broad neutralizers during AHI and associated with later neutralization breadth. V2 T cells decreased early in AHI, linked to viral load, while V1 expansion occurred in chronic infection. CD6 on V1 T correlated with early Env-specific IgM production. These findings suggest γ T cells may promote bAb development, informing HIV vaccine strategies targeting these cells to enhance humoral responses.
Researchers developed a computational model of bispecific antibody BS1 targeting IL-6R and IL-8 receptors to inhibit cancer metastasis. Using ordinary differential equations (ODEs), simulations show BS1 efficacy depends on receptor ratios; 1:1 IL6:IL8 yields monos inhibition. Ternary complexes guide design, optimizing bispecific therapies.
ZYG-8, a conserved doublecort-family kinase, regulates microtubule dynamics and motor activity in *C. elegans* oocytes to stabilize acentrosomal spindles. Depletion causes spindle elongation, midspindle defects, and excess outward forces, implicating BMK-1/kines5 regulation. ZYG-8’s kinase activity is essential in meiosis and mitosis, modulating microtule growth/nucleation rates and motor-driven forces. These dual roles—microtubule turnover and force tuning—ensure bipolar spindle stability, critical for faithful meiosis. Findings highlight mechanisms balancing forces in acentros spindles and ZYG-8’s role in cell division, with mammalian homolog linked to cancer.
This study explores the relationship between circulating metabolites, genetics, and type 2 diabetes (T2D) using UK Biobank and Estonian Biobank data. Mendelian randomization identifies 9 metabolites causally linked to T2, mostly lipid-related, while twice as many are affected by T2 liability, including branched-chain amino acids. Interaction QTL analysis reveals4 metabolites with altered genetic regulation in T2 cases, not linked to T2 risk. Differential analysis finds15 metabolites associated with T2 complications, some independent of T2 causality. Results highlight T2's impact on metabolite levels and regulation, offering insights into disease progression and complications.
Crossing MRSA-susceptible CC01 and tolerant CC4 mice revealed F1/F2 survival of 5% with dominant inheritance. Chromosome7 QTL with CC4's WSB allele and C5/C5 variants suggests altered C5 binding reduces cytokine storm, enhancing tolerance.
This study investigates how gene regulatory networks influence adaptive evolution using simulations comparing additive and network-based models. Both showed fewer large-effect beneficial mutations than expected, but the network model exhibited a bimodal fitness effect distribution with many deleterious alleles, slowing adaptation. Nonlinear gene interactions constrained trait evolution, contrasting traditional additive assumptions. Results highlight that genetic networks generate complex, multimodal fitness landscapes, altering adaptive trajectories and rates, suggesting gene interactions significantly shape evolutionary dynamics beyond classical models.
The study proposes a Bayesian framework where apical dendrites encode priors and basal dendrites likelihood in conductance-based neurons, enabling somatic posterior computation via gradient plasticity, explaining multisensory integration and testable predictions.
Using ECOD, researchers classified 8 AlphaFold proteomes (9% residues). Eukotes show more disordered regions; shared domains (e.g., Rossm/TIM). Structural predictions bridge sequence-classification gaps, aiding future strategies.
BK polyomavirus (BKPyV) relies on host cell S-phase replication for T antigen (TAg) expression and viral production, challenging the model where TAg initiates S-phase entry. Single-cell analysis shows robust TAg and viral replication depend on prior host S-phase, with BKV inducing G2-to-S re-replication (bypassing mitosis/G1) to achieve >4N DNA content. Host replication machinery drives re-replication, aligning BKV with other DNA viruses like papilloma/adenoviruses. Late genes (VP2/3) follow TAg in re-replicating cells, forming virions post-4N. Findings redefine BKV’s life cycle: TAg requires initial S-phase, replication occurs during re-rep, offering targets for antiviral therapies.
FAB is a TWAS fine-mapping method for binary traits that jointly models all genes on a chromosome using a probit regression to account for genetically regulated expression (GRe) correlations, enhancing power and reducing false discoveries. Simulations and UK Biobank analyses show FAB outperforms existing methods (FOCUS/FOG), shrinking causal gene sets by 7.9–69% and identifying genes like GATA3 (asthma), ABCG (gout), SH23B (hypertension). Its MCM algorithm scales to large datasets, leveraging GRe across LD blocks to improve precision.
Btn2 and Hsp2 sequeases are essential for oxidative stress tolerance by sequestering oxidized proteins into PQC sites, preventing aggregation. Mutants exhibit increased aggregates and toxicity; H14 overexpression rescues. Sup5 is a substrate; [PS+] prion forms without IPOD. Sequestration mitigates oxidative damage.
This study identifies long non-coding RNAs (lncRNAs) critical to glioblastoma (GBM) invasion using CRISPR-interference (CRISPRi). A CRISi-based screen of 2,37 lncRNAs revealed 48 significantly reducing invasion by 3–3% (p<0.01), with LINC0005 as top candidate. LINC005 knockdown reduced invasion by2.7% and correlated with poorer patient survival and tumor grade (p<0.000). RNA-seq linked LINC05 to WASF3, a known invasion mediator; WAS3 knockdown decreased invasion, while overexpression rescued L05’s effect. LINC05, a novel lncRNA, regulates GBM invasion via WAS3, suggesting therapeutic potential. Clinical relevance is supported by TCGA and GTEx data. This is the first large-scale CRISi screen of lncRNAs in GBM, highlighting L05 as a target for anti-invasive therapy.
The study investigates how the brain constructs probabilistic models of auditory sequences by analyzing EEG data from participants exposed to stimuli generated by a stochastic context-driven chain. A novel clustering method grouped EEG signals by their statistical patterns, revealing that the brain leverages recurrent auditory regularities to infer the underlying sequence-generating model. The stimuli were structured via a context tree with transition probabilities, and the clustering identified these patterns in EEG, suggesting the brain selects models based on observed regularities. This approach bypasses prior assumptions about specific model classes, instead extracting the structure directly from data. Findings indicate the brain uses frequent stimulus occurrences to deduce the stochastic model governing sequences.
This study addresses limitations of single-cell RNA-sequencing (scRNAq) in solid tissues by introducing cell-specific weighting-factors (cWF) to correct transcriptome size and dissociation-induced biases. cWFs computed for6 cell types across10 organs improve bulk RNAq reconstitution and deconvolution using scq data, validated via experimental and computational methods. cWF correlate with mRNA content and predict aging, suggesting diagnostic and mechanistic relevance. The approach enhances scq analysis of complex tissues and highlights cWF utility in biology and diagnostics. (1030 words)
Radial Mendelian randomization (MR) and multivariable MR (MVMR) address pleiotropy by using genetic variants as instrumental variables to estimate causal effects of exposures on outcomes. RadialMR identifies pleiotropic outliers via radial plots, while VMR extends to multiple exposures. This study introduces RadialVMR, a method combining radial visualization with VMR to detect and remove SNPs violating MVMR assumptions, reducing bias from pleiotropy. The RMVR R package implements RadialVM, enabling visualization of exposure-specific effects, heterogeneity, and outlier pruning of influential SNPs. Simulations and applications (e.g., lipid fractions on coronary heart disease) demonstrate RadialVM’s efficacy in mitigating bias and improving causal estimates. RadialVM provides diagnostics for MVM assumptions, enhancing robustness of causal inference in GWAS-based analyses.
Researchers continuously tracked *Drosophila melanogaster* behavior for up to 7 days at 10 Hz using SLE pose estimation, identifying stereotyped actions like grooming, proboscis extension, and locomotion. Daily patterns revealed circadian rhythms, with distinct morning/evening grooming differences and a post-dawn period linked to health metrics like locomotion speed. Behavioral decline over days mirrored circadian weakening, aligning with aging. High-resolution data highlights unexplored mechanisms in timescale interactions.
This study identifies the conserved non-receptor tyrosine phosphatase PTP-2 in *C. elegans* as a regulator of molting, cell adhesion, and cytoskeletal dynamics. Loss of PTP-2 phosphat activity suppresses molting defects in *nekl-2/3* mutants (homologs of human NEK6/7/8/9), suggesting antagonistic or pathway interactions. Proximity labeling revealed DNBP-1 (human DNMBP), a CDC2 GEF, as a PTP-2 interactor; DNBP loss similarly suppresses *nekl* defects. PTP-2 localizes to epidermal adhesion complexes (e.g., hemidesmos) and germl granules, implicating it in tissue integrity and nucleocytoplasmic transport/mRNA regulation. Over 30% of PTP-2-proximal proteins are germl gran components. Combined genetic and proteomic approaches uncover P-2’s roles beyond immunity, highlighting its conservation and multifunctionality in development.

NLRP1 and CARD8, FIIND-containing inflammasome proteins, form autoinhibitory NT-CT and FL-CT complexes via distinct mechanisms. Murine NLR1b uses Linker3 for NT-CT, while rat NLR1/CARD8 rely on Z5. DPP9 interacts with NTs (via Z5) and CTs, forming NT-DPP-CT and FLPP-CT complexes in rodent NLR1/CARD8 but not human NLR1. DPP facilitates NT-CT complex formation but does not modulate inhibitory activity. Autoproteolytic cleavage generates FL, NT, CT forms; pathogen proteases degrade NT/FL to activate inflamome. Structural diversity and DPP interactions highlight regulatory complexity in innate immunity.
Rer1, localized in the endoplasmic retic reticulum (ER) and Golgi, regulates proteostasis in Drosophila wing epithelium. Loss of rer1 induces proteotoxic stress via PERK-mediated eIFα phosphorylation, marking cells as "losers" eliminated by competition. Myc overexpression upregulates R1, mitigating stress to support overgrowth. R1 maintains proteostasis and competitive survival.
Researchers used deep mutational scanning to assess 4,87 CHEK2 variants in yeast, identifying70 damaging and2,47 non-synonymous SNVs that impair CHK2 function. Results align with structural data and prior assays, providing a scalable method to classify variants of uncertain significance in clinical databases, enhancing cancer risk prediction for CHEK2 and potentially other genes.
Streptococcus pneumoniae generates epigenetically and phenotypically distinct subpopulations via Spx1-TA toxin-antoxin (TA) system regulation of hsdS inversions in the opacity-determinant locus. Spx1 represses tenA transcription; spontaneous AT-dinucleotide variations in the spxA-ten promoter alter TenA levels, which bind ribosome factor RimM to reduce sigma ComX, upregulate psrA, and favor transparent-phase hsd alleles. This programmed genetic switch drives epigenomic shifts (e.g., DNA methylation patterns) and colony phase (opaque/transparent), enabling adaptive diversity. The S1-TA system, a novel type II TA, modulates bacterial biology through transcriptional control and toxin activity, linking epigenetic plasticity to pathogenesis.
Generalized contrastive PCA (gcPCA) is a hyperparameter-free method for symmetric comparison of high-dimensional datasets, solving cPCA's issues and enabling discovery of condition-specific patterns in neurophysiological and single-cell data.
This study establishes a semi-quantitative model of BCR signaling in Burkitt lymphoma cells, revealing feedback and crosstalk (e.g., p3 to ME/ER) conserved across B-cell lymphomas. The BL2-derived network applies to BL4 and DLCL lines with aberrant BCR, showing motifs preserved despite dysregulation. Phosphoproteomics validate interactions, suggesting common mechanisms. Novel connections (mTOR-JNK, GSK-ZAP, p8-RAFME) enhance fit. Findings imply BCR aberrations don’t majorly rewire downstream networks, aiding cross-lymphoma insights.
The study reveals that Notch1 receptor activity during angiogenesis is regulated by DLL4 and JAG1 ligands through distinct mechanisms: DLL4 promotes transactivation, while JAG1 antagonizes DLL4 by forming heteromeric JAG/DLL4 complexes that relieve cis-inhibition. Experimental and computational models demonstrate that JAG/DLL heteromers enable efficient Notch signaling, driving tip and stalk cell differentiation essential for sprouting. This challenges prior assumptions of homomeric ligand interactions, proposing a revised DLL4/JAG-Notch-VEGF model integrating Notch and VEGF signaling. Findings highlight heteromer formation as critical for angiogenic patterning, advancing understanding of Notch dynamics in vascular development. (10300 words)
The study introduces Dirichlet Process Mixtures with Uncertainty (DPMUnc), a Bayesian clustering method accounting for data uncertainty, applied to GWAS and gene expression data, showing improved disease clustering and signature analysis.
Deep networks often prioritize color/texture over shape in classification. This bias arises from gradient descent dynamics, not architecture. Altering learning algorithms could enhance shape sensitivity, aligning with primate vision.
Researchers developed a Kappa-based multiscale model of hepatic stellate cell (HSC) dynamics during liver fibrosis and reversion, revealing TGFβ-regulated activation/reactivation loops sustain fibrosis while inactivated HSC (i) accumulate in chronic disease. Validated with mouse models and NASH RNA data, identifying iSC as fibrosis markers. First model integrating SC heterogeneity, applicable to other tissues. (10 words)
Researchers developed a meta-analysis framework to estimate mediation effects of high-dimensional omics mediators using summary statistics, accounting for inter-study heterogeneity, applied to TOPMed data on blood pressure and HDL cholesterol, available in R package MetaR2.
The study introduces PWH, a method to identify personalized cancer driver genes by analyzing mutated genes' impact on expression in cohorts with shared mutations and expression profiles. PWH outperforms existing methods in detecting general and tumor-specific drivers across six TCGA cancers, validated by cell assays showing LRP1's role in proliferation, enhancing tumor stratification and treatment insights into heterogeneity.
The Virtual Epileptic Patient (VEP) model integrates patient-specific anatomical data with dynamical systems to simulate seizure patterns akin to stereoelectro-EEG recordings, enabling pre-surgical hypothesis testing. This study employs SaCeSS, a parallel metaheuristic global optimizer, to calibrate VEP parameters efficiently, outperforming existing solvers in scalability and accuracy. Enhanced via Bayesian hyperparameter tuning and uncertainty quantification, the method improves estimation of epileptogenic networks in drug-resistant epilepsy, aiding clinical decision-making.
Tuberculosis (TB), caused by Mycobacterium tuberculosis (Mtb), remains a major health issue. This study tracks H888 strain with plasm p0 in rabbits. Plasm stability in H8 higher than H3v. Non-monotonic plasm increase suggests subpopulations with replication/death. Granul dynamics imply heterogeneity. Rabbits differ from mice in Mtb.
GlycanModeler is a computational tool that predicts glycan structures using statistical models derived from the Protein Data Bank and quantum calculations, building glycans layer-by-layer with high accuracy for de novo and density-guided modeling. Benchmarked on glycans of varying lengths, it achieved median accuracy of 2.7 Å RMSD. Applied to design glycans on nanoparticles to shield protein regions from antibodies, experimentally validated. Enhances glycoprotein modeling, structure determination, and design by enabling accurate de novo glycan prediction and integration into experimental data, advancing computational biology and vaccine development.
The E3 ubiquitin ligase SCFFbx3 in *Penicillium oxalicum* regulates the transcription factor Ace1 (PoAce1) via ubiquitination, modulating fungal development and cellulase gene expression. PoFbx3, the F-box subunit, exists predominantly free in the nucleus but forms SCFF3 complexes with Skp1, Cul1, and Rbx1. Under glucose, PoF3 deletion (Δfb3) reduces brA and pigmentation gene expression, impairing conidiation; under cellulose, it upregulates (hemi)cellulase genes. Po1, ubiquitinated by SCFF3, exists as full-length and degraded forms. Δfb3 causes Po1 accumulation, which loses promoter binding to cellulase (cbh1, eg1, xyn1A) and pigmentation (abrB) genes. Po3 acts as a coactivator, enabling Ace1 to repress or activate genes depending on signals, revealing SC3’s role in substrate-specific transcriptional regulation.
The study reveals that in *Drosophila melanaster* follicular epithelium, basement membrane (BM) diversification arises from parallel Rab1 and Rab8-dependent secretion routes. Rab1 mediates lateral, planar-polarized secretion of fibrils, while Rab8 drives basal secretion of homogenous matrix. Dystrophin-associated complex (DAP) colocalizes with Rab1, promoting fibril formation and redirecting secretion to Rab1. Exoc complex has dual roles: Exo7 subunit limits dystrophin polarization, and supports Rab8. BM diversity emerges from spatial control of these routes integrated with cell axes. Disruption of Rab/Rab blocks BM but partial redundancy exists. DAP absence shifts secretion to Rab8, forming homogenous. Exoc is essential for homogenous. Mechanism shows BM diversification via distinct secretory routes and polarity.
A machine learning model, LBUM, was developed to predict HIV-1 resistance to broadly neutralizing antibodies (bnAbs) using multi-task learning (MTL), addressing challenges of underrepresented subtypes and combination resistance. Trained on diverse data, LBUM mitigated subtype bias and identified co-resistance patterns, enabling epitope prediction and optimal bnAb selection. Outperformed classical methods like random forests and gradient boosting. Publicly available, it offers tools for HIV and other antibody-treated diseases. (1298 words)
Pathway-based models, particularly group lasso incorporating immune-related VAX pathways, outperformed gene-based models in predicting multiple myeloma prognosis using microarray data (GSE3334) and external validation. Three scoring methods (ssGSEA, GSVA, z-scores) and four databases were tested, with VAX grp showing robustness to <5% missing data via imputation. Immune pathways aligned with myeloma biology; models available in R package (https://github.com/Shuo/MMMs) for reproducibility.
Researchers developed a nonlinear model of Drp1-dependent mitochondrial fission to identify regulatory mechanisms. Total fission rate (T) undergoes Hopf bifurcation with μ = k+M -k, representing oligomer assembly/disassembly. Cumulative fission (TF) non-monotonically increases with μ, peaking then decreasing, suggesting interventions on k+, k−, or M may have non-intuitive effects. This highlights μ as key for fission regulation, informing therapies. (30 words)
CRISPR-based gene drives targeting the recessive fertility gene *TyrAmine decarboxylase 2 (Tdc)* in *Drosophila suzii* and *Drosophila melanogaster* were developed to suppress pest populations. A 3-gRNA system induced mutations in *Tdc*, but germline homing was limited; however, octopamine restored egg-laying in mutants, enabling line maintenance. Split systems with promoter-Cas9 improved homing efficiency in *D. melanogaster*. Wild polymorphisms hindered drive spread, and Cas9 activity varied by genomic position. Conditional rescue of female infertility via octamine feeding offers scalable production of transgenic insects. This approach mitigates resistance by targeting constrained regions and allows reversible sterility, enhancing gene drive utility for pest control.
The brain's energy for learning is constrained by computation and memory. Experiments show simple tasks have metabolic costs, MN requiring at least 8 synaptic updates. Two algorithms: modify large synapses, restrict paths. Over-dimension networks use more; restricting saves energy with trade. Aligns biological and artificial learning, efficiency.
Researchers engineered *Acinetobacter bayly* ADP-IS strains with genome deletions, causing fitness defects. Laboratory evolution over 30 generations in different media restored fitness via mutations in regulatory genes (*rnc, csrA, hfq*), showing recovery through deletion-specific and global adjustments. Most strains improved; two failed in one environment. Demonstrates lab evolution recovers genome streamlining fitness.
The study introduces RiboFlip, a T34 self-cleaving ribozyme-based system for endogenous gene regulation in zebrafish. Insertion of T34 ribozyme in introns reduced mRNA levels up to 2-fold, outperforming other ribozymes. CRISPR/Cas-mediated insertion in *alb* gene replicated mutant pigmentation, reversible via base-edit inactivation. RiboFlip, Flipp/Cre-inducible, replicated *al* phenotype and enabled Gal4/UAS reporter labeling independent of target expression. Demonstrates T4 ribozyme efficacy in vertebrates, expanding conditional knockdown tools. (13030 words)
The study introduces aiSEG, a user-friendly CNN-based software for nuclei segmentation in brightfield without fluorescent labeling. Evaluated on 1.1 million nuclei across 2,00000 images, it achieves accuracy comparable to manual methods in challenging conditions like low magnification and time-lapse. Requires 2 images for retraining, accessible via CLI/GUI, no coding. Retains biosensor data, reduces phototoxicity.
Humans exhibit a bias toward learning reward-predictive features that change slowly, leveraging a "slowness prior" in reinforcement learning. In two experiments and a preregistered replication, 25 participants learned two-dimensional bandits where reward was predicted by a slowly or quickly changing feature. Participants accrued more reward when the relevant feature changed slowly and irrelevantly quickly. Kalman filter models revealed higher learning rates for slow features, with adjustment to relevance and speed. Performance improvement correlated with learning rate adjustment. Generalization to new stimuli was equal across conditions. Results suggest humans adapt learning rates to feature dynamics, favoring slower processes, aligning with slown prior in causal inference.
This study identifies Resf as a novel tumor suppressor gene in estrogen receptor-negative (ER) breast cancer. Using mouse genetics, researchers found that reduced Resf expression correlates with increased tumor growth, faster progression, and more lung metastases in PyMT mouse models. Human data align with these findings, showing lower Res1 expression linked to worse outcomes. Mechanistically, Resf appears to regulate transcription via G-quadruplexes, affecting ribosomal biogenesis. Loss of Res1 enhances tumor progression through transcriptional and translational changes. These results highlight Resf as a potential therapeutic target for ER- breast cancer.
The study investigates the roles of Mec1 and Rad4 in meiotic recombination in *S. cerevisiae*. Mec1 and Rad4 regulate DNA double-strand break (DSB) formation and repair, with Rad4 deletion (rad4Δ) reducing spore viability and recombination frequency due to shortened prophase, while Mec1 loss (mec1n) increases recombination. Both mutants exhibit elevated multi-chromatid events from closely spaced DSBs, indicating impaired DSB spatial regulation. Mec and Rad4 also govern crossover (CO) interference: their loss randomizes CO distribution, resembling but less severely than ZMM mutants like zipΔ. Rad4 acts as a pro-C factor, while Mec regulates recombination frequency, mitigating CO defects from DDR ablation. High-resolution mapping reveals shared and distinct roles in DSB/CO regulation. Prophase extension via Ndt8 improves spore viability in mutants. Results clarify Mec’s role in DSB interference and Rad4 in CO regulation, highlighting their interplay in meiotic fidelity. (1300 words)
Establishing in vitro culture conditions for *Pneumocyst jiroii*, a deadly fungal pathogen causing severe pneumonia in immunocompromised individuals, has long hindered research due to its unculturable nature. This study presents the first genome-scale in silico metabolic model of *Pumocyst* growth, integrating genomic data and bioinformatics to identify metabolic requirements and imbalances limiting in vitro growth. Using Flux Balance Analysis and Reinforcement Learning, critical components of Meral’s medium for *Pumyst* were predicted, suggesting supplements to enhance growth. The model replicated gene knockouts and drop experiments, aiding antifungal target development. A parallel model for *Pumocyst murina* (mouse pathogen) validated hypotheses, as human testing is infeasible. Findings offer insights into *Pumyst* biology and a strategy to overcome culturing challenges, addressing a major bottleneck in diagnosing and studying this pathogen reliant on microscopic detection. The work bridges data gaps in *Pumyst* physiology, enabling future experimental validation and drug design.
A 3D computational model integrating cell dynamics and the Hippo-YAP/TA pathway reveals that doubling YAP/TA levels in cancer cells enables sustained proliferation under high-density conditions by evading contact inhibition, unlike normal cells. The model simulates cell interactions via molecular dynamics (adhesion, repulsion, friction) and Lennard-Jones potentials, showing increased Y/TA overcomes Hippo-mediated arrest. Findings suggest Y/TA elevation alone drives malignancy, offering a tool for evaluating cancer progression and optimizing Y/TA-targeted therapies.
The study introduces an energy framework using stickiness and Wasserstein distance to analyze low-complexity domains (LCDs) in biomolecular condens. Periodic LCD patterns enhance elasticity, random increase viscosity. Minimum periodic prevents solid transitions. FELS model explains prion visco, sequence governs material. Advances dynamics, evolution.
The study demonstrates that Sonic Hedgehog (Shh) signaling drives epithelial invagination in tooth development by activating myosin II via the PI3K/AKT pathway, which strengthens cell-cell adhesion at adherens junctions and enables convergent cell movements in the suprabasal layer. Myos II is essential for maintaining adhesion and force generation; its disruption impairs epithelial narrowing and invagination. Pharmacological AKT/myos II activation rescues defects caused by Shh inhibition, establishing a Sh-PIK/AKT-Myo axis critical for epithelial morphogenesis. Results highlight myos II’s dual role in adhesion and force generation, aligning with prior findings on its role in junction stability. Future work will explore contributions of specific junction types (adherens, tight, desmosomes) to cellular rearrangement.
The study introduces scGC, a deep graph convolutional network for transferring labels from single-cell RNA to chromatin data, improving multi-omics integration by preserving heterogeneity. Efficiently handles large datasets, cross-species, and modalities, outperforming existing methods in annotation.
Researchers characterized the nuclear localization signal (NLS) of Mcm3, a replicative helicase subunit, using mutagenesis and AlphaFold3. Specific basic residues at positions 2 and3 in Mcm3’s NLS are critical for importin interactions, enabling nuclear import and chromatin loading. Disrupting these residues impairs MCM complex assembly and growth. Despite lacking a consensus sequence, Mc3 and SV40 T NLS share structural features, offering a framework for monopite NLS prediction. AF3 models interactions but some mutants (e.g., Mcm3SV0-NLSR) show discrepancies. Mc3 lacking NES is constitutively nuclear. Impaired import hinders MCM loading, causing growth defects. Study provides structure-guided insights for NLS analysis. (103 words)
Ataxin-2 (ATX2) is involved in neurodegenerative diseases like spinocerebellar ataxia type 2, ALS, and Parkinson's. It regulates mRNA translation, stability, and RNP-granule assembly via intrinsically disordered regions. The LSm domain antagonizes RNP-granule formation, while the PAM motif interacts with polyA-binding protein to recruit mRNAs and proteins into Atax-2 granules. Experiments in Drosophila show the LSm domain may protect against neurodegeneration, while PAM and IDRs contribute to cytotoxicity. Findings suggest Atax-2 interactions remodel during translation, with structured and unstructured regions affecting RNP condensation and neurodegeneration.
The study investigates gene regulatory networks governing skeletal muscle stem cell (MuSC) development and maintenance in extraocular muscles (EOM) versus limb muscles. Temporal inactivation of Pitx2 and Pax7 reveals distinct roles: Pitx2 is critical early in embryonic myogenesis but dispensable for postnatal EOM MuSC maintenance, while Pax7 loss reduces EOM MuSCs more severely than limb. EOM MuSCs enter quiescence earlier, remain non-proliferative in adults, yet harbor higher Pax7+ density. In Duchenne dystrophy (mdx model), EOM MuSCs are fewer and non-proliferative compared to limb. Findings highlight anatomical heterogeneity in MuSC dynamics and mechanisms underlying EOM resistance to dystrophy.
Researchers developed a VOC-INN, integrating an SI1R model and physics-informed neural networks (PINs), to simulate SARS-Co-2 variants in British Columbia, accurately fitting data, simulating observed/unobserved dynamics, inferring time-dependent parameters, and revealing regional control strategy variations. Effective for long-term multi-wave analysis, it combines epidemiological data and machine learning, leveraging ODEs and PIN to capture time-vary transmission dynamics of VOCs.
This study introduces CytoNet, a Deep Sets-based model that improves aggregation of single-cell image profiling data via self-supervised contrastive learning, enhancing mechanism-of-action prediction by 3–8% over averaging. CytoNet applies contrastive learning to pre-extracted morphological features, not raw pixels, enabling use in existing datasets. It aggregates cell sets per sample, prioritizing non-mitotic, non-debris cells for quality control. Requires only perturbation labels, common in profiling data. Outperforms prior methods, offering a post-processing boost for image-based profiling. Future utility in genetic perturbations and functional genomics.
The study introduces a framework to quantify cognitive effort using EEG microstate dynamics and optimal transport theory, applied to a spatial Stroop task dataset. Results show increased transition costs correlate with cognitive demand, validating the method's efficacy. First EEG-based application offers a novel, data-driven approach to physiologically describe cognitive effort, bridging gaps in neurophysiological quantification. (1300 words)
This study investigates the role of atypical memory B cells (aBCs) in the humoral immune response to *Plasmodium vivax* malaria. PvDBI-specific aBCs were detected during and persisted post-infection, with some producing neutralizing antibodies comparable to classical MBCs. Single-cell cultures revealed aBC-derived antibodies with broad reactivity against PvDBI variants. aBCs expressed similar IGH genes and SHM to classical MBC. Findings suggest aBC contribute to protective immunity by differentiating into antibody-secreting cells, highlighting their potential for vaccine development.
The study introduces mr.mash-rss, a method for polygenic prediction of complex traits using summary statistics from genome-wide association studies (GWAS) and linkage disequilibrium (LD) data instead of individual-level genotypes, addressing privacy and scalability limitations of the original mr.mash model. By leveraging shared effects across phenotypes, mrash-rss improves prediction accuracy for single and multi-phenotype scenarios, outperforming existing methods in simulations and real-world analysis of six blood traits in the UK Biobank, particularly with smaller sample sizes. The approach enables application to non-public datasets and large biobanks, demonstrating robustness to missing data and varying heritability, offering a scalable solution for precision medicine and genetic research.
Researchers developed a model integrating spatio-temporal heterogeneity into epidemic predictions using Universal Differential Equations (U) with neural and mechanistic models. Applied to Shanghai’s Omron outbreak, the model projected 8.6% more accurate attack rate (8.0 vs.9%) and peak (3.7 vs.28%) than homogeneous. Heterogeneity reduced herd immunity by7.3% and prolonged outbreaks by7 days, aligning data. Enhances accuracy by accounting for heterogeneity, offering new method.
This study proposes that synaptic noise encodes uncertainty about postsynaptic somatic activity via an internal model updated by LTP/LTD plasticity. Synapses act as agents in dynamic environments, using release variability to represent uncertainty. Network coordination enables tasks like classification and control by resolving ambiguities. Predict synaptic stochasticity and plastic in post-pre pairing.
Scup is a distance-based lineage reconstruction method using bulk and single-cell DNA, addressing scDNA challenges like allelic drop and amplification. It uses neighbor-joining, is parallel, efficient, accurate, validated on synthetic and 8 data. Designed for healthy tissues with scarce mutations, leveraging read-ph to distinguish somatic.
The study introduces the individual-based Thanzi Lase (TLO) model to evaluate Malawi's health benefit packages (HBPs) under resource constraints, simulating health gains from prioritization strategies. A linear optimization (CO)-based HB achieved ∼8% DALY reduction by 2024 but initial excess DALYs, while patient-characteristic-based prioritization offered 5% reduction with consistent annual gains. The TLO model integrates realistic healthcare capacity, time requirements, and status quo factors, addressing limitations of prior methods. Future work will expand on additional factors. This approach provides a data-driven tool for Malawi's resource-constrained healthcare planning. (1300 words)
This study investigates meiotic chromosome dynamics in the holocentric moths *Plodia interpunctella* and *Bomby mori* using Oligo-FISH, revealing conserved homolog pairing initiation at gene-rich chromosome ends and cruciform bivalent formation at metaphase I. Unlike *Bomby*, *Plodia* exhibits non-telomeric kinetochore assembly at chromosome centers, with four distinct, unpaired kinetochores at metaphase I. Microtubule attachments co-orient these kineto, challenging classical models requiring paired pole-facing kineto for homolog segregation. Findings suggest a novel "center-kinetic" mechanism in moths, emphasizing non-model species for uncovering meiotic diversity. (10303 words)
The study demonstrates that SOX3 deficiency in the median eminence (ME) disrupts NG2-glia proliferation and oligodendrocytic differentiation, leading to postnatal hypituitarism via impaired pituitary endocrine maturation. Low-dose aspirin or altered gut microbiota rescues NG2-glia proliferation and hormonal deficits but not myelination, indicating NG2-glia’s critical role in post-weaning pitary development. CNS-specific SOX loss causes hypit, with SOX expressed in hypothalamus, not pituit. NG2-glia numbers in ME are essential for pitary maturation, and their function is modifiable by non-genetic factors.
The study in *C. elegans* identifies CED-5/CED-2 as a dual-function protein complex regulating F-actin dynamics during morphogenesis. While CED-5/CED2 acts as a GEF to activate CED-1/Rac for corpse engulfment and DTC migration, it paradoxically inhibits F-act in epidermal embryonic migrations. A GAP domain in CED-2, distinct from its GEF region, suppresses F-act during epider morphogenesis, with mutations in CED2’s GAP (R37A) disrupting epider but not engulf. Genetic data suggest CED-5/C2 regulates multiple GTPases via distinct domains, promoting and inhibiting F-act in context-specific processes. This reveals CED-5/C2’s role in balancing GEF and GAP activities to control F-act for development.
The study uses information-theoretic and autocorrelation analysis to show that in the rodent visual system, information and timescales increase along the anatomical hierarchy while predictability decreases. Spontaneous activity shows a similar timescale hierarchy, but predictability is stimulus-dependent. A recurrent model replicates this, suggesting intrinsic mechanisms like coupling enable longer integration in higher areas, reducing predictability for efficient coding.
Transcranial magnetic stimulation (TMS) is a non-invasive, FDA-cleared treatment for neuropsychiatric disorders with broad potential new applications, but the neural circuits engaged during TMS remain poorly understood. This study used epidural recordings from the cervical spine to develop a computational model of a motor macrocolumn to investigate TMS response mechanisms, including direct and indirect waves. Sensitivity analysis identified key pathways and neuron types contributing to corticospinal waves, showing that single wave preference correlates with average connection probability to L5 pyramidal tract neurons (PTNs) and conduction delay of the shortest path to L5 PTNs. Multiple neuron types modulate specific corticinal waves, with both excitatory and inhibitory involvement. Afferents and cortical neurons initiate I-waves, suggesting cortical afferent origins for certain I-waves. The methodology enables computational analysis of complex models to understand acute stimulation mechanisms.
Cell-free placental DNA (cfDNA) circulates in maternal blood during pregnancy, originating from the placenta and detectable as early as the fourth gestational week, comprising up to 4% of total plasma cell-free DNA. It enables non-invasive prenatal testing (NIPT) for fetal chromosomal aneuploidies (e.g., Trisomies 3,8,13) by analyzing overrepresented chromosomes in maternal plasma. cfDNA reflects the placental genome, distinct from fetal DNA in cases of placental mosa, offering non-invasive insights into placental genetics. Despite clinical use in NIPT, its biological origins and functional roles remain poorly understood, limiting broader applications. Research is needed to elucidate placental processes generating cfDNA, its role in pregnancy, and potential for monitoring placental health and disease, expanding beyond current genetic screening to longitudinal studies of placental development and pathology.
Genome-wide studies reveal clustered risk variants in hormone-dependent cancers (breast, endometrial, ovarian, prostate), identifying multi-cancer regions, genes, lncRNAs, and drug targets, suggesting shared mechanisms and therapeutic repurposing.
Researchers identified a 9 kb deletion upstream of IL2/IL2 in Kiker dogs with polymyos, linked via GWAS and sequencing. The deletion, present in8% of cases vs5% controls, disrupts gene regulation, causing overexpression upon stimulation. Homozygous dogs have2% risk, heterozyous0.5%. Findings suggest similar mechanisms in human autoimmune diseases. A PCR aids breeders to reduce incidence.
Researchers developed ESMm, a protein language model for stability prediction, trained on 58k sequences from 41 domains, handling mutations. Fine-tuned from ESM2, it predicts small domains' stability, generalizes distal. Lags on larger; more data. Training domains improve mutagen. Highlights large datasets.
Inhibitory killer immunoglobulin receptors (iKIRs), expressed on natural killer (NK) cells and late-stage T cells, modulate immune responses by binding HLA class I ligands. In Type 1 diabetes (T1D), a study of 1911 cases found iK genes significantly reduced protective HLA class II genetic associations, validated in an independent dataset. This suggests iKs regulate CD4+ T cell activity in autoimm, contrasting their role in chronic infections where they enhance T responses. iK-HLA interactions, like KIR3DL-HLA-B, modulate adaptive immunity, with iK diminishing HLA II’s protective effect in T1. Findings imply iKs suppress CD4 T-mediated autoimmunity, potentially synergizing with NK cells to prevent disease. This highlights iK’s dual role in immune regulation, balancing viral defense and autoimm.
Fuchs endothelial corne dystrophy (FE), a leading cause of age-related vision loss, is linked to CTG8.1 expansions in TCF. Using corne endothelial cells from Exp+ and Exp- FECD cases, this study employs long-read, short-read, and spatial transcriptomics to reveal expansion-driven splicing, TCF isoform dysregulation, and gene expression. Exome data identify rare TCF variants in 7/14 Exp- cases, suggesting two mechanisms: RNA toxicity and TCF dys underpin pathophysiology, guiding interventions.

longer. example.
Hepatitis B virus (HBV) relaxed circular DNA (rcDNA) contains terminal redundancy (TR) on the negative strand, with the 5’ TR serving as template for positive-strand synthesis, forming a duplex, while the3’ TR forms a flap removed during covalently closed DNA (ccDNA) formation. A C82G mutation in pregenomic RNA (pgRNA) revealed wild-type nt122 dominance in rcDNA and cDNA, confirming 5 TR retention. Next-generation sequencing and RACE-NG identified Mus8 and FEN1 as flap endonucleases cleaving3’ and5’ TR, respectively, with overlapping roles indicating dynamic flap interchangeability. This elucidates HBV rcDNA structure and cDNA mechanisms, critical for replication understanding viral persistence. (1300 words)
This study uses a microbe-micro genome-scale metabolic model to analyze microbial communities in microbial fuel cells (MFCs) treating sulfide wastewater. Three guilds—sulfate-reducing bacteria (SR), methogens (MET), and sulfide-oxidizing (SO)—shift from SO-dominant to MET-dant as organic loading (OL) rises, reducing FC performance. The model predicts microbial abundances, showing SO constrained by sulfate-sulf cycling and acetate crossfeeding under high OL, favoring MET. Crossfeeding dynamics reveal acidity impacts, highlighting crossfeeding’s role in structuring communities for FC optimization.
The article presents CPEC, an ML framework integrating deep learning and conformal prediction for FDR-controlled enzyme annotation. It mitigates overconfidence by quantifying uncertainty, ensuring FDR within user limits. Effective on underrepresented enzymes, outperforming existing methods. Useful for resource-limited discovery.
Neuronal inclusions of hyperphosphorylated TDP-43 are hallmarks of amyotrophic lateral sclerosis (ALS). Mutations in TARDBP cause familial ALS, indicating TDP-4 dysfunction drives disease. Aggregated TDP-4 may contribute to pathology or be protective. Using a *C. elegans* model of TDP-4 proteinopathy, loss of HSP-9 protects against TDP-4 toxicity and neurodegeneration, reducing total and phosphorylated TDP-4. HSP-9 inhibition upregulates stress genes hsp-7 and hsp-6.1; normal hsp-6.1 is required for HSP-9 effects. Neuroprotection does not involve proteasome activity. HSP9 contributes to adverse outcomes in TDP-4opathies in vivo.
Researchers used single-nucle RNA and chromatin accessibility sequencing to map Artemia francana’s reproductive system, identifying conserved cell types with Drosophila and revealing Z chromosome meiosis dynamics and meiotic silencing in a non-model arthropod.
Chronic pain, including allodynia (pain from non-painful stimuli), is linked to dysregulated excitatory-inhibitory (E-I) balance in spinal dorsal horn circuits. This study models biophysically-motivated subcircuits in lamina I-II to identify mechanisms underlying static and dynamic allodynia. Using firing rate models of excitatory/inhibitory neurons, they find E-I imbalance arises via inhibitory downregulation (releasing excitation) or excitatory upregulation (escaping inhibition). Subcircuit structure determines mechanism likelihood, components, and prevalence, explaining interindividual variability. Results suggest diverse mechanisms for allody etiology, offering hypotheses for experimental validation and therapeutic targets.
Hsp90 and cochaperones H1, Cns, and Cpr regulate eukaryotic elongation factor 2 (eEF2) function through distinct mechanisms. Mutations in Hsp0 or cochones reduce e2 levels and alter diphther toxin sensitivity, indicating roles in folding and posttranslational modification. Yeast H1 deletion exacerbates e2 mutant defects, while H1 overexpression partially rescues some. Hsp0 mutants show isoform-specific effects, correlating with cochone subsets, suggesting distinct folding pathways. e2 isoforms (EFT1/FT2) and H0 isoforms (HSC2/HSP2) vary in interaction. H0 contributes to proteostasis via translation accuracy, not just folding, and interacts with TRC chaperone via H1. Results highlight H0’s dual role in elongation and initiation, with implications for targeted inhibition.

Biomorphs, computational models of morphological evolution, exhibit phenotypic bias where simpler phenotypes with lower descriptional complexity are orders of magnitude more likely to arise via random mutations. This bias, explained by an information-theoretic principles, influences adaptive evolution: common phenotypes fix despite lower fitness, mirroring molecular genotype-phenotype maps. Simulations reveal mutational robustness, evolvability-robustness correlation, and "arrival-of-the-frequent" effects. These patterns suggest developmental systems may universally exhibit simplicity bias, akin to molecular scales, though empirical validation in broader contexts remains challenging.
Researchers investigated whether humans intuitively exploit resonance in nonlinear systems by controlling a virtual double pendulum via haptic interface. Participants alternately hit targets aligned with or offset from numerically predicted nonlinear normal modes (NM) of energy-conservative systems. Across three experiments, users stabilized motions near NM despite damping, adjusting arm stiffness to align resonant dynamics with tasks. Even when targets deviated from NM (Experiment 3), participants adapted strategies to achieve goals, suggesting active shaping of system dynamics. Findings demonstrate human sensitivity to nonlinear resonance, extending beyond linear systems, through adaptive control and stiffness modulation. Results highlight intrinsic capability to exploit resonant motions in complex interactions.
In *Bacillus subtilis*, the transition state regulators ScoC and AbrB, along with the MarR-family factor PchR, repress the biosynthesis of the iron chelator pulchimin during exponential growth by regulating the *yvmC* gene, which encodes a key biosynthetic enzyme. Genetic and in vitro analyses reveal that ScoC, AbrB, and Pch bind the *yvmC* promoter, with Sco exhibiting weak direct repression, while Pch and AbrB impede RNA polymerase progression. This layered regulation restricts pulchimin production to stationary phase, linking iron sequestration to nutrient transitions. The interplay of these repressors ensures precise control of pulchimin, critical for bacterial physiology during growth shifts.
A computational model of spinal neural circuits using Hodgkin-Hux equations replicated post-SCI bladder dysfunction and transcutaneous magnetic stimulation (TMS) effects. Low-frequency TMS (1 Hz) normalized voiding, high-frequency (3 Hz) enhanced storage. Neuroplasticity and interne interactions critical for TMS efficacy.
This study introduces a mathematical model to estimate morphology-specific fungal growth rates of *Aspergillus fumatus* using optical density (OD60) data without requiring calibration. Traditional methods rely on labor-intensive morphological measurements like hyphal length, which are impractical for clinical labs. The model treats OD6 as an indirect measure of true fungal concentration, integrating calibration within its structure to avoid de novo data collection. Applied to OD6 time-course data, it outperforms existing models in fitting and predicting growth curves, resolving discrepancies between OD-inferred and direct measurements. By linking OD6 to biologically interpretable rates, it enables accessible, scalable fungal growth quantification for labs lacking specialized tools. The approach addresses filamentous fungi’s unique OD sensitivity to size/shape, where bacterial calibrations fail, offering a practical solution for clinical microbiology. (10303 words)
Beetles, the most species-rich animal group, exhibit diverse karyotypes with XY/X0 sex determination. Using *Tribolium castaneum*’ whole-chromosome assembly and 111 genomes, researchers reconstructed Coleoptera kary evolution. Ancestral X chromosomes (Stevens elements) are conserved, but neo-sex chromosomes form via autosomal additions, showing dosage compensation and sex-bi gene distribution. Beetles model sex chromosome evolution forces.
Researchers investigated the role of histone variant H2A.Z in *Saccharomyces cerevisiae* under hydroxyurea (HU)-induced stress by analyzing mRNA profiles of *htzΔ*, *swrΔ*, and *htswΔrΔ* mutants. H2.Z primarily facilitates gene activation rather than repression during HU, crucial for upregulating HU-induced genes. Apo-SWR-C (SW without H2.Z) contributes to expression defects in *htz* mutants, notably in phosphate homeostasis. H2 occupancy at transcription sites decreased with HU but wasn’t essential for upreg. H.Z’s transcriptional role is context-dependent, especially under stress. (10303 words)
The study addresses automated classification of single-cell transcriptomic profiles using partial label learning, where each data point receives a set of candidate labels instead of one. Methods like SVM, kNN, logistic regression, and ensemble were adapted, emphasizing hierarchical label structures common in developmental processes. Nonlinear prototype-based methods achieved high accuracy, matching fully supervised models on real/simulated data. Uncertainty analysis showed performance trade-offs. Partial learning reduces annotation needs, enabling efficient scRNA-seq annotation.
Phosphatidylinositol 4,5-bisphosphate (PIP2) localizes to nuclear compartments like speckles, nucleoli, and lipidlets in an RNA-dependent manner. Using mass spectrometry, the RNA-dependent PIP-associated (RD) proteome was identified, revealing intrinsically disordered regions (IDRs) with polybasic PIP-binding motifs and posttranslational modifications. BRD4 associates with PIP2 via electrostatic interactions, with PIP levels altering BR4 foci. PIP spatially orchestrates nuclear processes via RNA and RD proteins, suggesting a role in phase separation and nuclear architecture for gene expression.
The study investigates the genomic basis of phenotypic plasticity in dung beetles (Scarabaeaeina), focusing on horn development and nutrition-responsive traits. Chromosome-level genomes of three Onthophagini species (Onthagus taurus, O. sagittarius, D. gazella) and comparisons with seven Coleoptera genomes reveal coding changes in metabolic and metamorphic regulation. Chromatin accessibility in developing horns of O. taurus shows distinct regulatory architectures for nutrition- vs. sex-driven development, with novel elements linked to horn morph determination. Transcription factor motifs are enriched in nutrition-responsive regions, highlighting chromatin's role in mediating plasticity. Results demonstrate evolvable gene networks transducing environmental signals and genetic inputs, providing reference genomes to advance developmental, ecological, and evolutionary research in this diverse clade. Non-synonymous substitutions in developmental genes suggest adaptive roles in horn evolution, a novel trait with extreme variation. Findings underscore non-coding genome's role in trait plasticity and diversification.
Lassa fever pathogenesis in cynomolg monkeys reveals lymphoid organs as early viral replication sites, with nonfatal cases restricting LASV to lymphoid tissues and immune cells, while fatal cases exhibit systemic dissemination to multiple organs, macrophage/neutrophil infiltration, and inflammation. Strains Josiah (fatal) and AV (nonfatal) induce distinct outcomes, highlighting immune responses and viral tropism as critical to disease severity. Animal models clarify mechanisms absent in human studies.

This study introduces a method to enhance CRISPR-Cas-mediated mutagenesis in lytic phages with cytosine DNA modifications by employing the eukaryotic NgET enzyme to temporally reduce 5mdC. Applied to T4 phage, it enabled scarless point mutations in ADP-ribylase genes (modA, alt), critical for infection, and revealed delayed lysis (20 min) in CRIS-C1_Alt-expressing E. coli. Temporal demethylation elucidated modification roles without gene deletions, offering a strategy to study phage epigenetics and engineer modified phages, advancing synthetic biology and infection mechanism research.
Histone variant H2A.Z is essential for transcription-coupled nucleotide excision repair (TC-NER) and genome stability following UV irradiation. In yeast, absence of H2.Z impairs TCER, reduces RNA polymerase II clearance, and increases double-strand breaks (DSBs). UV-irradiated H2-depleted cells accumulate DSBs, highlighting its role in preventing genome instability. H2.Z, conserved from yeast to humans, is linked to DNA repair, checkpoint, DSB resolution, and replication. Its deposition via SWR complex is critical for TCER. Defective H2 response leads to sustained DSBs and genomic instability. Findings emphasize chromatin environment in DNA repair.
This study examines gene expression and microbiome variation in *Drosophila melanogaster* midgut, hindgut, and Malpian tubules from African and European populations, revealing tissue-specific trans effects dominate cis, indicating spatially fine-tuned regulatory evolution during divergence.
Researchers developed a population-dynamics model to estimate SARS-CoV-2 and Alpha emergence using early cases. Simulations validated. UK first infection median Aug1202000 (9%PR July-Sept), Wuhan Nov21 ( Nov-Dec). Results align genomic. Method for outbreaks.
Researchers developed an agent-based model to elucidate homolog pairing during meiosis, incorporating attractive forces between homologs and repulsive forces dissociating non-homologs. Simulations reveal that repulsive interactions reduce non-homolog associations, confining homologs to limited nuclear areas, enabling subsequent homolog attraction. Chromosome number, size, velocity, and repulsive strength govern pairing efficiency. The model recapitulates wild-type and mutant yeast meiosis kinetics and adapts to diverse organisms. Pairing arises from two processes: non-hom dissociation via repulsion and hom attraction in confined spaces.
Li-Fu syndrome, caused by TP3 mutations, involves miR-3a as a tumor suppressor gene. Zebraf miR-3a and mi-3b are p5-dependent under DNA damage, with mi-3a more abundant. mi-3 loss accelerates tumors in TP3 mutants, despite normal p5 responses. mi-3a affects hematopoiesis and sensitizes to camothec, not γ-irradiation. Transcriptomic changes reveal mi-3’s role in development and tumor suppression, conserved in humans. Epigenetic silencing of MIR4 in TP3 carriers worsens cancer. miR-3a overexpression modulates DNA damage response but not p5 targets.
The nematode *C. elegans* uses the XOL-1 protein to regulate sex determination and dosage compensation based on the X:autosome ratio. While XOL-1 is highly expressed in males, it is present at low levels in hermophrodites. This study reveals XOL-1 also regulates developmental timing in hermophite embryos. Loss of xol-1 leads to accelerated cell division, advanced transcription, and early activation of dosage compensation and sex pathways. XOL-1 controls H3K9 methylation via MET-2, and loss of met-2 reverses some xol-1 effects. Thus, X-1 is a key regulator in both sexes, with MET-2 acting as a downstream effector in hermophrodites.
MGSurv is a computational framework optimizing trap placement for mosquito genetic surveillance to minimize allele detection time. It integrates biological factors: resource distribution, mosquito movement (sex, gonot cycle, resource), trap attractiveness. Applied to Aedes aegypti (Queensland) and Anopheles gambia (São Tomé), MGS prioritizes early detection of gene drive spread, resistance, or insecticide resistance alleles. Uses spatial optimization via genetic algorithms, considering local ecology and dispersal patterns. Demonstrates utility for gene drive monitoring and resistance tracking, enhancing surveillance efficiency. Designed for field-computational collaboration, with open documentation. Early detection critical for effective intervention, mirroring invasive species lessons. Key for scalable, cost-effective mosquito control strategies. (10000 words)
Symbionas scillans, a 1.4-μm heterotrophic eukaryote previously reported to host endosymbiotic bacteria, lacks detectable endobacteria via amplification-free metagenomics, whole-genome sequencing, and FISH. Instead, prasinovirus contigs related to Ostreoccus, Bathycoccus, and Micromonas viruses were identified, with near-complete 10-kb genomes assembled. Transmission electron microscopy revealed 0-nm virus-like particles matching original endosymbion morphology. Results confirm S. scill associates with praviruses, not endobacteria.
The leiomodin (Lmod) family of actin-binding proteins is essential for muscle function, and mutations in LMOD genes cause myopathies, including severe neonatal dilated cardiomyopathy from LMOD2 mutations. Most mutations are nonsense or frameshift, leading to truncated proteins, but often with little or no LMOD expression due to nonsense-mediated decay (NMD) of mutant mRNAs. This study shows NMD underlies protein loss in two L2 mutations and demonstrates that steric-blocking oligonucleotides can inhibit NMD, restoring mutant L2 expression. These findings suggest potential therapeutic strategies for L-linked myopathies.
Apolipoprotein E (Apo) polymorphisms influence Alzheimer’s disease (AD) risk, with Apo4 increasing and Ap2 decreasing it. In transgenic mice expressing human Apo isoforms (2,3,4), brain proteome homeostasis analysis revealed Ap4 and Ap2 alter mitochondrial protein regulation. Ap4 disrupts proteas/autophagy, reducing protein quality; Ap2 enhances matrix/membrane degradation, suggesting organelle replacement. Liver shows no changes, highlighting brain-specific effects. Combining abundance and turnover reveals proteost mechanisms linked to AD.
Researchers developed a CRISPR-mediated tissue-restricted mutagenesis (CRIS-TRM) toolkit to enable tissue-specific gene knockout in Drosophila neuromuscular junction (NMJ) motoneurons, muscles, and glial cells, overcoming prior limitations of CRISPR in this system. CRIS-TRM was validated via multiple gene knockouts, compatibility with Gal4/UAS, and simultaneous targeting redundant genes. It revealed SNARE proteins’ essential role in NMJ maintenance, ESCRT pathway’s suppression of NMJ growth via downregulating retrograde Gbb signaling, and ESCRT-mediated axonal trafficking for extracellular vesicle release at NMJs. This approach identified genes critical for NMJ structural plasticity, demonstrating CRISTR’s utility in dissecting NMJ biology.
Drosophila hematopoiesis relies on larval lymph gland progenitors primed by reactive oxygen species (ROS), which activate JNK to upregulate fatty acid oxidation (FAO) for differentiation. The NF-κB factor Relish restricts premature differentiation by inhibiting TAK, thereby dampening JNK-FA signaling in ROS-enrich progenitors. Relish expression declines as cells differentiate, releasing TAK inhibition and allowing JNK-driven FAO. This balances progenitor maintenance and differentiation, ensuring ROS-primed cells are not exhausted. Relish’s dual role in immune response and hematopoiesis highlights metabolic-NFκB integration in developmental cell fate control.
A patient with Taybi-Linder syndrome (TALS)-like features but no pathogenic RNUATAC variants was found to carry a homozygous RTTN c.25A>G variant. Functional studies in fibroblasts, RPE cells, and CRISPR-edited iPSC-derived neural stem cells revealed RTTN mutations cause mitotic abnormalities, aneuploidy, cell cycle arrest, and delayed neural roset formation in cortical organoids, linking RTTN dysfunction to microcephaly and growth defects. RTTN c.5A>G disrupts splicing, altering centrosome/cilium functions and NSC self-organization.
Escherichia coli adapts to prolonged resource exhaustion in long-term stationary phase (LTSP) through convergent genetic mutations over six years, with lineages defined by shared RNA polymerase mutations emerging across populations. Convergent lineages exhibit similar dynamics, and 30% of mutated loci show significant mutational associations, indicating historical contingency. Parallel adaptation and lineage structure enable identification of contingent loci pairs, revealing frequent interdependencies. Mutations persist beyond chance, diminishing over time, highlighting LTSP as a model for studying evolutionary convergence and contingency in non-sporulating bacteria.
The male-specific MSA RNA in *Drosophila melanogaster* encodes a micropeptide (MSAmP) regulating sperm usage in mated females, while the CNS-expressed iab-8 lncRNA lacks translation due to repressive upstream open reading frames (uORFs) in its 5’ exons. Transgenic and cell culture studies show these uORs block downstream translation, explaining why i-8ncRNA’s intronic miRNA (mi-i8) functions without protein production. MSA and i-8 share exons beyond the first, but MSA’s unique 5’ end enables MSAmP expression in male accessory glands, whereas i-8’s uORs prevent CNS translation. This mechanism ensures tissue-specific regulation of MSA and i-8 functions. (13030 words)
Congenital disorders of glycosylation (CDG), caused by mutations in glycosylation pathways, present with variable multisystem symptoms including seizures and developmental delays. This study leveraged evolutionary rate covariation (ERC) to identify common genetic modifiers across CDG by analyzing conserved glycosylation proteins from yeast to mammals. ERC revealed strong evolutionary links within and between glycosylation pathways, ncRNA modification, DNA repair, and subcellular localization of GPI enzymes. Functional testing validated top candidates as CDG modifiers, including known genes like PMM2-PGM and novel interactions (e.g., PIGB-UTP20, PIGN-WDR6). High ERC scores suggest shared constraints and potential therapeutic targets. Evolutionary analysis prioritizes modifiers, offering insights into pathophysiology and therapies for CDG.
Hepatitis B virus (HBV) core (HB) phosphorylation at Ser2/7 initiates RNA encapsulation; dephorylation by Pol-recited PP1 at Ser7, via Val8 domain and RNA, completes packaging. HBV dual role in RNA delivery and PP1 recruitment highlights PP as antiviral target. (0 words)
The study investigates how bacterial symbionts in chemosynthetic bivalves adapted to environmental changes after the Isth of Panama closure by comparing endosymbion genomes from sister species in the Caribbean (CAR) and Tropical Pacific (TEP). Metagenomic analysis revealed nitrogen fixation genes (nifDK operon) in CAR symbionts but not TEP, despite similar phylogeny, indicating convergent evolution in nutrient-poor CAR. Ancestral reconstruction showed Ca. Thiazotro lacked nif genes, later acquired via horizontal transfer from Sedicola symbion in oligot habitats. This HGT enabled diversification of Ca. Thiazro, highlighting nitrogen’s role in ecological speciation and symbion-driven adaptation to environmental shifts. Findings underscore symbionts’ importance in host resilience to environmental change. (12999 words)
This study identifies 9992 TASRs from6 vertebrates, revealing amphibians (frogs, salam) have expanded TASR clusters and higher counts than other lineages. TASR numbers correlate with extraoral expression; in vitro show amphibian TASRs detect ecologically xenob as chemos. Phylogen suggests recombination drives TASR diversity, subfunctional extraoral.
