Background selection in structured populations reduces neutral diversity (πT) and differentiation (FST) via linked deleterious alleles. This study extends theory to include migration in an island model, distinguishing two regimes: background (strong selection, low mutation) and interference (weak, high). Migration reduces FST when rates exceed selection (m ≥ t), truncating cross-generational associations. Simulations confirm high migration minimizes FST but lowers πT, especially in larger populations. Background weakly confounds FST scans under high gene flow. Theoretical advances complex demography.
FedGAT is a privacy-preserving federated GWAS tool using generalized mixed models, enabling secure aggregation of encrypted statistics across sites without data sharing, matching pooled results in simulations and real data.
This study evaluates six polygenic risk score (PRS) algorithms for prostate cancer prediction in UK Biobank and All of Us cohorts, finding modest improvements over clumping-based methods. Algorithms include variant prioritization, shrinkage, joint analysis, annotation, fine-mapping, and population-specific heritability. First pan-ancestry analysis in All Us shows hierarchical clustering stratifies PRS by ancestry. Age+PRS improves prediction; family history/BMI less impactful. PRS+PSA screening may reduce overdiagnosis but requires equitable cross-ancestry performance to address disparities. Diverse cohort sampling and algorithm refinement critical for equitable risk prediction.
Researchers used a *Drosophila* model of DPAG1-CD, a congenital glycosylation disorder, to screen 1,50000 FDA-approved drugs, identifying four candidates that improved eye defects. Dopamine D2 receptor inhibition and reduced dopaminergic flux partially rescued the model, linking dopamine signaling to N-glycosylation. Acetylcholine, COX, and NKCC inhibitors also showed efficacy, revealing novel therapeutic targets for DP1-CD. Genetic validation confirmed drug mechanisms, highlighting dopamine-D2 and other pathways as potential treatments.
Researchers developed a topographic variational autoencoder (topo-VA) model to infer cortical representations of proprioception from natural human arm movements, without neural data fitting. The model replicates two key findings from monkey studies: hand-centered proprioceptive field shapes/velocity profiles and neuronal preferred direction (PD) distributions. It predicts cortical PDs exhibit blob-and-wheel geometry and sparse joint encoding. The model offers a framework for sensorimotor representations, neural manifolds, and applications in brain-computer interfaces and robotics. Proprioceptive coding principles derived from kinematics may generalize across species.
Azospirillum brasilense possesses a functional ethylene receptor (Azo1) that binds ethylene, reducing biofilm and root colonization. Ethylene induces metabolic shifts, including polyhydrobutyrate accumulation. Host ethylene alters bacterial colonization density and rewires metabolism, offering targets for regulating plant-microbe interactions.
The INO8 chromatin remodeler facilitates meiotic sex chromosome silencing in murine pachene spermatocytes by localizing at the XY body and recruiting DNA repair factors (ATR, M1) to double-strand break (DSB) sites, enhancing chromatin accessibility independent of histone H2 Z. Ino deletion leads to elevated sex-linked gene expression, active RNA polymerase II, and reduced meiotic silencing initiators, indicating INO’s role in DNA repair-facilitated silencing. Chromatin accessibility, critical for repair and transcription, is diminished without INO, impairing sex chromosome silencing during zygon-to-pachema transition. INO’s interaction with M1 and ATR amplifies γH2AX signaling, promoting DSB repair and silencing, distinct from its autosomal H3K73me regulation. These findings establish INO as a key regulator of chromatin dynamics for meiotic sex chromosome inactivation.
Cytidine deaminase CDD2 (CDD2) facilitates axon regeneration in *Caenorhabditis elegans* by converting SVH-1, a dual-function protein with protease and growth factor activities, from a protease to a growth factor. SVH-1, containing a catalytic triad (Asp–His–Ser), promotes axon regeneration via HGF-like signaling but also acts as a plasmin-like protease in development. Mutation of His-75 to Tyr in SVH-1’s catalytic triad suppresses *cdd-2* defects in axon regeneration, and a hairpin structure around His-75 in *svh-1* mRNA is critical for this activation. CDD2 modifies *sv-1* mRNA, altering SV-1’s function, enabling its growth role in regeneration while suppressing protease activity. This mechanism explains SV-1’s switch from protease to growth factor, essential for axon repair post-injury. Genetic and RNAi studies confirm CDD2’s specificity in this pathway, distinct from JNK signaling. Results reveal mRNA editing by CDD2 as a regulatory switch for SV-1’s dual roles. (13030 words)
Researchers genetically modified zebraf to study collective behavior via active matter models. Col1 gene knockout caused vertebral defects, reduced body bending, slower orientation. Surprisingly, mutant groups showed increased order. Modeled self-prop agents with higher orientational noise, demonstrating bottom-up control of biological systems through genetics.
A hybrid computational model integrating mechanical and chemical cues was developed to simulate in vitro capillary network formation. The Cellular Potts model predicted endothelial cell migration and morphology, while continuum equations quantified biogel deformation and vascular endothelial growth factor (VEGF) transport. Soluble VEG induced morphological changes, and bound VEG on the biogel surface provided directional signals, both essential for network integrity. Simulations showed elongated cells formed cords and round cells created cobblestone aggregates, aligning with experiments. Capillary networks required simultaneous mechanical-chemical coupling: biog deformation, sufficient bound VEG, and its gradient. Prior models lacked full coupling, e.g., missing bound VEG’s role or biel tilt effects. This study highlights dual regulation’s necessity for capillary development.
The study reveals that all five TGF-β ligands in *C. elegans* (DBL-1, DAF-7, UNC-19, TIG-2, TIG-3) contribute to survival against bacterial pathogens, with non-redundant interactions between subfamilies. BMP-like DBL-1 and TIG-2 act independently, while TIG-2 (BMP) and TGF/Activin-like TIG-3 function synergistically, supported by structural heterodimer modeling. TIG-2 and TIG-3 lack a conserved cysteine for disulfide bonds. DBL-1/BMP signaling via Smads mediates immune response, whereas DAF7/Activin pathways do not. This highlights cross-subfamily collaboration in innate immunity, distinct from developmental roles, suggesting novel mechanisms for pathogen defense.
This study identifies the N-terminal acetyltransferase Nat4 as a novel regulator of the DNA damage response in *Saccharomyces cerevisiae*. Nat4 acetylates the N-terminus of histone H4 and is recruited to double-strand breaks upon DNA damage. Cells lacking Nat4 show increased sensitivity to DNA damage, accumulate more breaks, and exhibit impaired checkpoint activation. Nat4 deficiency reduces γH2A levels, Rad9 recruitment, and Mec1 kinase activity, essential for damage signaling. The effects depend on Nat4’s acetylase activity toward histone H4. This work links Nat4 to DDR, highlighting a new histone-modifying role in genome integrity.
Orchard is a novel algorithm for reconstructing cancer phylogenies from bulk sequencing data, overcoming limitations of existing methods that fail beyond ~30 mutations. It employs factorized posterior approximation and sequential optimization to build phylogen incrementally, achieving accuracy up to 1000 mutations. Evaluated on 9 simulated cancers and4 B-progen acute lymphoblastic leukemias, Orchard outperforms Pairtree and CALDER, reconstructing trees with up to1000 mutations. Large phylogen enable identification of somatic mutation patterns and subclonal heterogeneity, aiding cancer progression understanding, driver discovery, and treatment. The method reduces pre-clustering needs, handles 10 samples, and scales to10-node trees in6 hours. Probabilistic refinements and downstream applications are anticipated.
This study introduces Immugen, a modular protein language model for CD8+ epitope immunogenic prediction. Trained on pMHC tasks with TCR integration, it outperforms existing models (AUC 0.69, AP.0.5) by 7%. Highlights dataset biases and interpretability.
This study identifies the protein phosphatase 1 catalytic subunit gamma (PPPCC) as a causative gene for meat color in chickens. Using GWAS, gene-based analysis, and Mendelian randomization, PPPCC was linked to lightness and redness. PPPCC knockout mice showed increased lightness, reduced myoglobin, and a shift from slow- to fast-twitch fibers. Transcriptome and metabolome data revealed PPPCC inhibition reduced slow-fiber genes and enhanced glycolysis. A SNP (rs15287) in PPPCC intron regulated gene activity. Differences in PPPCC expression, rs127 variant, and fast-twitch markers were observed between fast white-feather and local chickens. PPPCC emerges as a target for meat improvement.
The study introduces super-resolved tomographic reconstruction (STR), a method combining super-resolution microscopy and tomography principles, to efficiently identify subunits within retinal ganglion cell receptive fields. By using Ricker-shaped stimuli and tomographic light patterns, STR resolves subunit layouts in simulations and primate parasol ganglion recordings, achieving reliable results in minutes. This enables rapid, targeted analysis of subunit properties, interactions, and retinal circuitry, facilitating closed-loop experiments. Validated experimentally via electrophysiologically in marmos retinas, STR reduces recording time, enabling real-time subunit characterization.
The study introduces CRISPR-DR, a statistical method integrating CRISPR interference (CRISi) and drug concentration data to identify chemical-genetic interactions (CGIs) by modeling non-linear interactions between sgRNA efficiency and drug sensitivity. CRISDR outperforms existing methods in precision by accounting for optimal intermediate sgRNA strength for synergy detection, validated in Mycobacterium tuberculosis and Escherichia coli datasets, reducing false positives in noisy data.
The study challenges the assumption of modularity in gene co-expression networks by applying the weighted degree-corrected stochastic block model (SBM), which does not enforce assortative grouping. Using Drosophila melanogaster RNA-seq data, the SBM identified tenfold more gene groups than modular methods, many non-modular, with functional enrichment comparable to modular clusters. Results suggest transcriptomes are hierarchically structured beyond modularity, necessitating non-modular approaches. Non-modular blocks’ functional relevance equals modular, urging reevaluation of network analysis methods. SBM’s flexibility reveals complex organization, highlighting limitations of prior assumptions. Future work should integrate network inference and community detection for robust insights. (1300 words)
Cytoplasmic poly(A)-binding protein 1 (Pab1) in yeast plays multiple roles in post-transcriptional regulation, including translation initiation, termination, and mRNA decay. Using mass spectrometry, RNA-Seq, and Ribo-Seq, this study shows that deletion of PAB1 (pabΔ) causes widespread changes in the proteome and transcriptome, with defects in translation initiation, termination, and mRNA stabilization. Reduced levels of initiation factors, decapping activators, and deadenylation components contribute to these effects. pabΔ cells exhibit nonsense codon readthrough, indicating termination defects. The loss of Pab is pleiotropic, disrupting multiple post-transcriptional processes. Proteomic data reveal direct and indirect consequences of PAB deletion, adding complexity to genome-wide gene expression in PAB-depleted cells. P1’s role in initiation is context-dependent, influenced by poly(A) tract and translation levels. Ribosome footprints in 5’UTR increase in pabΔ, suggesting altered cap-independent initiation.
The study demonstrates that interactions between extracellular potassium dynamics and the Na+/K+-ATPase in class I neurons can generate slow rhythms via hysteresis and bistability. Pump strength determines bursting, tonic spiking, or depolar block. Glial dysfunction or hypox may disrupt this, linking to epilepsy. A minimal model offers insights for therapies.
The COPS package evaluates multi-view clustering for cancer subtyping by integrating multiomics data (mRNA, CNV, miRNA, methylation) across seven cancers. It compares data- and pathway-driven methods using ARI, survival analysis, and stability. Affinity Fusion, NMF, and Pathway Kernels excel. Multiobjective Pareto analysis identifies optimal subtypes with prognostic value. Adjusts for covariates, ensures robustness via subsampling. Addresses prior gaps in systematic comparison and covariate-adjusted survival. 10303 words.
SEM-2, the sole *C. elegans* SoxC protein, regulates dorsoventral M lineage patterning by antagonizing LET-8, ensures SM fate specification, proliferation, and diversification, and directly controls *hlh8* expression. A DNA-binding domain mutation reveals SEM2’s role in conserved SoxC-Twist interactions and postembryonic GRN.
